  [HEADER]
  /*
  * gurfeater.pc -- mainline for gurfeater Banner interface program.  This
  * program implements the collection and processing of Banner GURFEED
  * interfaces through a table-driven approach.  The program requires two
  * tables to be living in the database:
  *
  * FZBIMPTH   -- one record per interface, keyed on SYSTEM_ID FZRIMPTD   -- one
  * record per input/target field, keyed on SYSTEM_ID and SEQ_NUM
  *
  * The program will query the database at start up to obtain the interface
  * specification based on the first line of input, which is assumed to
  * contain several fields used to control the processing:
  *
  * SYSTEM_ID       -- used as look up in our tables BATCH_DATE      -- used as
  * activity date for our run REC_COUNT       -- used as a control element to

  [HEADER]
  /* datastore.h -- store data in a place allocated on the fly. */
  /* DataStores are used to keep data in variable-like objects.  Since we
  * will be processing multiple record types, with different mixtures of
  * datatypes, we will use malloc at program startup to define our storage
  * based on the column specifications.
  */
  /*

  [HEADER]
  /*
  * docexec.c -- table of function pointers used in the processing of columns
  * and rows.
  *
  * This module uses POINTERS TO FUNCTIONS, which is not a common construct in
  * most C programs.  It is also not a novice technique.  You may have to do
  * some studying to understand what is going on here.  I cite "The C
  * Programming Language" by Kernighan & Richie--the sort program in this book
  * uses this technique.  You might also want to look at the man page for
  * "signal" to see another use.
  *
  * Essentially, a pointer to a function is declared with:
  *
  * int (*funcptr)();
  *

  [LMOD BLOCKS]

    Line 106: --    make sure the document total on the jv header equals the total

    Line 113: --    accompllish the edit. fgrtrni sets the 'process context' to

  #           then grepped at end to assess and report errors.  This final grep command both used

    Line 91: # AUDIT TRAIL: 8.0
    Line 92: # 1. Apply 7.5 modifications to 8.0
    Line 93: #
    Line 94: # AUDIT TRAIL: 8.1
    Line 95: # 1. LVH 06 Jun 2008
    Line 96: #    RPE:     1-2DGZLW
    Line 97: #    Problem: The umask value of 000 allows full read and write capability
    Line 98: #             for user, group and world.
    Line 99: #    Solution:Depending on how your environment is set up, you may wish to
    Line 100: #             change the delivered values set by umask.
    Line 101: #
    Line 102: #    If jobsub and the users are in different groups you may need to use
    Line 103: #    umask 000. If they are in the same group you could use 017. If all
    Line 104: #    reports are run to the database and server access is not required then
    Line 105: #    you could use 077.
    Line 106: #
    Line 107: #    To change the default permissions assigned to your UNIX files and
    Line 108: #    directories, use the umask command. Its format is
    Line 109: #        umask nnn
    Line 110: #    where nnn is a three-digit code that defines the new default permissions.
    Line 111: #    The umask string does NOT have the same format as the chmod permission
    Line 112: #    string.
    Line 113: #
    Line 114: #    Each of the three numbers represents one of the categories user, group,
    Line 115: #    and other. The value for a category is calculated as follows:
    Line 116: #        read permission has a value of 4
    Line 117: #        write permission has a value of 2
    Line 118: #        execute permission has a value of 1
    Line 119: #
    Line 120: #    Sum the permissions you want to set for the category, then subtract that
    Line 121: #    value from 7. As an example, examine the current default umask statement
    Line 122: #    that is used to assign the file protections -rwx-r-x--- :
    Line 123: #        umask 027
    Line 124: #    The user category value is 0 because r+w+x = 4+2+1 = 7. When this is
    Line 125: #    subtracted from 7, the value is 0.
    Line 126: #    The group category value is 2 because r+x = 4+1 = 5. When this is
    Line 127: #    subtracted from 7, the value is 2.
    Line 128: #    The other category value is 7 because no permissions = 0. When this is
    Line 129: #    subtracted from 7, the value is 7.
    Line 130: #
    Line 131: #    For example:
    Line 132: #
    Line 133: #       umask 000        Set default to allow full access to everyone
    Line 134: #       touch test.000   Create file test.000 showing the resulting permissions
    Line 135: #       umask 017
    Line 136: #       touch test.017
    Line 137: #       umask 022
    Line 138: #       touch test.022
    Line 139: #       umask 027
    Line 140: #       touch test.027
    Line 141: #       umask 077
    Line 142: #       touch test.077   Allows access to only the owner
    Line 143: #       ls -l test.*    (execute access (x) does not display for non-executables)
    Line 144: #         -rw-rw-rw-   Jun 12 12:04 test.000
    Line 145: #         -rw-rw----   Jun 12 12:05 test.017
    Line 146: #         -rw-r--r--   Jun 12 12:05 test.022
    Line 147: #         -rw-r-----   Jun 12 12:05 test.027
    Line 148: #         -rw-------   Jun 12 12:05 test.077
    Line 149: #
    Line 150: #    It is important to note that files created by the jobsub process are not
    Line 151: #    the same as the user if for whom the process is being run. For example, if
    Line 152: #    saisusr submits glolett then glolett_12345.log and glotlett_12345.lis will
    Line 153: #    be owned by the account running jobsub, NOT saisusr. If reports are run
    Line 154: #    to the database and viewed by gjirevo, then this may not be an issue.
    Line 155: #    However, if the reports needs to be accessed on the server then it may be.
    Line 156: #
    Line 157: #    To determine which group a user is in, use the command: id <username>
    Line 158: #    i.e. id user001
    Line 159: #         uid=6356(user001) gid=401(banner)
    Line 160: #

FILE: local_shl\gzrparm.shl
----------------------------------------
  [HEADER]
  #!/bin/bash
  # gzrparm.shl 11/12/08 Mark J Penniman
  #
  # script dedicated to defining the banner job submission access and parsing functions
  # script included in parent (like TSV extract scripts )at run-time to define the functions
  # used to get banner job subsubmission parameters from table gjbprun.
  # this file is designed to be a fragment of a larger script and to be included in the
  # larger script by using ". gzrparm.shl" in the script, the ksh "include".
  #
  # OP20090211_gzrprnt function was capitalizing parms. OK for TSV but not for GZRPRNT. fixed
  # FPT-3828 -jk/mjp 3/2018- syntax changes for embedded SQL statements
  #
  # FUNCTION DEFINITIONS -------------------------------------------------------------------
  #set -x

  [LMOD BLOCKS]
    Line 61:      /* job_name and one_up are values used to select desired parameters */
    Line 62:      define job_name = $2
    Line 63:      define one_up = $3
    Line 64: 
    Line 65:      select  gjbprun_number, TRIM(upper(nvl(gjbprun_value,'ALL')))
    Line 66:      from    general.gjbprun
    Line 67:      where   gjbprun_job = '&job_name'
    Line 68:      and     gjbprun_one_up_no = &one_up;
    Line 69: 
    Line 70:      exit
    Line 71: SQLPLUSEOF
    Line 72: )`; export PARM
    Line 73: fi
    Line 74: PARM=`echo $PARM | sed 's/Connected.//'`
    Line 75: }
    Line 76: 
    Line 77: function get_a_parm
    Line 78: {
    Line 79: # $1 is parameter number to return, $2 is string containing all parameters
    Line 80: # $IDX contains the element number of the array that represents the location
    Line 81: #   of the parameter to be returned
    Line 82: #
    Line 83: # LMOD OR20081010_Extract_Email_O10g start
    Line 84:   ((IDX=($2 * 2) )); export IDX     # method A - example: parameter position = 6 = ((3) * 2), "Connected" does not start string

    Line 378:                          and fabinvh_cancel_date is null )

  [HEADER]
  /* fzpdwx3.sql		Verification of nightly FIS-to-DWH extract.  This   */
  /*				is run as part of production script frundwhxtrc.		*/
  /* 05/15/03 - dlk:  Initial creation.                                   */
  /* 09/27/11 - mjp:  expand F01-F06 format from 11 to 17                 */

  [LMOD BLOCKS]
    Line 4: /* 09/27/11 - mjp:  expand F01-F06 format from 11 to 17                 */
    Line 5: 
    Line 6: WHENEVER SQLERROR EXIT SQL.SQLCODE rollback
    Line 7: whenever oserror  exit oscode rollback
    Line 8: SET ECHO     OFF
    Line 9: SET TERMOUT  OFF
    Line 10: SET FEEDBACK OFF
    Line 11: SET SHOWMODE OFF
    Line 12: SET TIMING   OFF
    Line 13: SET TIME     OFF
    Line 14: SET VERIFY   OFF
    Line 15: 
    Line 16: set head off
    Line 17: 
    Line 18: col  lit						fold_a
    Line 19: -- LMOD FPT-1523 start
    Line 20: col	F01	format 999,999,999,999,990.00	fold_a
    Line 21: col	F02	format 999,999,999,999,990.00	fold_a
    Line 22: col	F03	format 999,999,999,999,990.00	fold_a
    Line 23: col	F04	format 999,999,999,999,990.00	fold_a
    Line 24: col	F05	format 999,999,999,999,990.00	fold_a
    Line 25: col	F06	format 999,999,999,999,990.00	fold_a
    Line 26: -- LMOD FPT-1523 end
    Line 27: 
    Line 28: select 'DWH transaction count: '|| count(*)
    Line 29: from   fgbtrnx,
    Line 30:        fzrdwhd
    Line 31: where  fgbtrnd_coas_code = 'X'
    Line 32: and    fgbtrnd_activity_date > fzrdwhd_prev_load_date
    Line 33: and    fgbtrnd_activity_date < fzrdwhd_last_load_date
    Line 34: /
    Line 35: 
    Line 36: select 'FIS transaction count: '|| count(*)
    Line 37: from   fgbtrnd,
    Line 38:        fzrdwhd
    Line 39: where  fgbtrnd_coas_code = 'X'
    Line 40: and    fgbtrnd_ledger_ind = 'O'
    Line 41: and    fgbtrnd_trans_amt != 0
    Line 42: and    to_number(fgbtrnd_field_code) <= 6
    Line 43: and    fgbtrnd_activity_date > fzrdwhd_prev_load_date
    Line 44: and    fgbtrnd_activity_date < fzrdwhd_last_load_date
    Line 45: /
    Line 46: 
    Line 47: select 'DWH Totals: '                   lit,
    Line 48: 		'Fld 01:  ',
    Line 49:           sum(fgbtrnd_budg_amt)         F01,
    Line 50: 		'Fld 02:  ',
    Line 51:           sum(fgbtrnd_adjbudg_amt)      F02,
    Line 52: 		'Fld 03:  ',
    Line 53:           sum(fgbtrnd_trans_amt)        F03,
    Line 54: 		'Fld 04:  ',
    Line 55:           sum(fgbtrnd_encumb_amt)       F04,
    Line 56: 		'Fld 05:  ',
    Line 57:           sum(fgbtrnd_reserv_amt)       F05,
    Line 58: 		'Fld 06:  ',
    Line 59:           sum(fgbtrnd_acctd_bud_amt)    F06
    Line 60: from   fgbtrnx,
    Line 61:        fzrdwhd
    Line 62: where  fgbtrnd_coas_code = 'X'
    Line 63: and    fgbtrnd_activity_date > fzrdwhd_prev_load_date
    Line 64: and    fgbtrnd_activity_date < fzrdwhd_last_load_date
    Line 65: /
    Line 66: 
    Line 67: select 'FIS Totals: '                    		lit,
    Line 68: 		'Fld 01:  ',
    Line 69:           sum(decode(fgbtrnd_field_code, '01',
    Line 70:                         fgbtrnd_trans_amt,0))  	F01,

    Line 92: /* Checks payable to payee name that includes "Larive" (used to be "Blumenthal" chanded 08/05/19) */
    Line 93: set heading off
    Line 94: set feedback off
    Line 95: select '------------------------------------------------------------------------'
    Line 96:   from sys.dual;
    Line 97: select 'Checks payable to payee name that includes "Larive"'
    Line 98:   from sys.dual;
    Line 99: select '------------------------------------------------------------------------'
    Line 100:   from sys.dual;
    Line 101: 
    Line 102: set heading on
    Line 103: set feedback on
    Line 104: column ckno format a16
    Line 105: column acct format a8
    Line 106: column payee format a30
    Line 107: column amt format 999,999,999.99
    Line 108: 
    Line 109: select  evibcchk_check_number ckno,
    Line 110:         evibcchk_account_code acct,
    Line 111:         substr(evibcchk_payee_name,1,30)   payee,
    Line 112:         to_number(evibcchk_amount) amt
    Line 113:    from evibcchk
    Line 114:    where UPPER(evibcchk_payee_name) like '%LARIVE%' and
    Line 115:          evibcchk_account_code <> '01' and
    Line 116:          trunc(evibcchk_activity_date) = TRUNC(&RDATE);
    Line 117: 
    Line 118: -- Overflow checks
    Line 119: set heading off
    Line 120: set feedback off
    Line 121: select '------------------------------------------------------------------------'
    Line 122:   from sys.dual;
    Line 123: select 'Overflow Checks'
    Line 124:   from sys.dual;
    Line 125: select '------------------------------------------------------------------------'
    Line 126:   from sys.dual;
    Line 127: 
    Line 128: set heading on
    Line 129: set feedback on
    Line 130: column ckno format a16
    Line 131: column acct format a8

  #!/bin/bash
  # sid_validate mjpenniman 6/2006
  # call-able script that validates a user entered ORACLE_SID code
  # see sid_valid file for a single edit point to add/subtract valid Oracle SIDs instead of in multiple scripts
  # 1 parameter - selected ORACLE_SID code. First element in array is default if no parameter supplied
  #                                         remember array cell numbering in korn shell scripts starts at 0

  #
  # use the 6 example lines as a guideline for calling this script from within another script
  #   note that the script is called using the ". " prepended. This prevents another shell from being started.
  #
  #1            . sid_validate.shl $1
